{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-08-19 22:02:03","updatedTime":"2020-08-19 22:02:03","title":"How to Autoload Classes With Composer in PHP","link":"https://code.tutsplus.com/tutorials/how-to-autoload-classes-with-composer-in-php--cms-35649","description":"<p>In this article, we’ll discuss the basics of autoloading in PHP and how to autoload PHP classes with Composer. I'll explain why autoloading is so important and show you how to use Composer for autoloading step by step. I'll also explain the difference between the different kinds of autoloading in Composer.</p><h2>Why Do We Need Autoloading?<br>\n</h2><p>When you build PHP applications, you may need to use third-party libraries. And as you know, if you want to use these libraries in your application, you need to include them in your source files by using <code class=\"inline\">require</code> or <code class=\"inline\">include</code> statements. </p><p>These <code class=\"inline\">require</code> or <code class=\"inline\">include</code> statements are fine as long as you’re developing small applications. But as your application grows, the list of <code class=\"inline\">require</code> or <code class=\"inline\">include</code> statements gets longer and longer, which is a bit annoying and difficult to maintain. The other problem with this approach is that you're loading the entire libraries in your application, including the parts you're not even using. This leads to a heavier memory footprint for your application.</p><p>To overcome this problem, it would be ideal to load classes only when they are actually needed. That's where autoloading comes in. Basically, when you use a class in your application, the autoloader checks if it’s already loaded, and if not, the autoloader loads the necessary class into memory. So the class is loaded on the fly where it’s needed—this is called autoloading. When you’re using autoloading, you don’t need to include all the library files manually; you just need to include the autoloader file which contains the logic of autoloading, and the necessary classes will be included dynamically.</p><p>Later in this article, we'll look at autoloading with Composer. But first, I'll explain how you can implement autoloading in PHP <em>without</em> Composer.<br></p><h2>How Autoloading Works Without Composer<br>\n</h2><p>You might not realize it, but it is possible to implement autoloading in PHP without Composer. The <code class=\"inline\">spl_autoload_register()</code> function is what makes this possible. The <code class=\"inline\">spl_autoload_register()</code> function allows you to register functions that will be put into a queue to be triggered sequentially when PHP tries to load classes that are not loaded yet.</p><p>Let’s quickly go through the following example to understand how it works.</p><pre class=\"brush: php noskimlinks noskimwords\">&lt;?php\nfunction custom_autoloader($class) {\n  include 'lib/' . $class . '.php';\n}\n\nspl_autoload_register('custom_autoloader');\n\n$objFooBar = new FooBar();\n?&gt;</pre><p>In the above example, we’ve registered the <code class=\"inline\">custom_autoloader()</code> function as our custom autoloader by using the <code class=\"inline\">spl_autoload_register()</code> function. Next, when you try to instantiate the <code class=\"inline\">FooBar</code> class and it’s not yet available, PHP will execute all the registered autoloader functions sequentially. And thus the <code class=\"inline\">custom_autoloader</code> function is called—it includes the necessary class file, and finally the object is instantiated. For this example, we're assuming the <code class=\"inline\">FooBar</code> class is defined in the <strong>lib/FooBar.php</strong> file.</p><p>Without autoloading, you would need to use the <code class=\"inline\">require</code> or <code class=\"inline\">include</code> statement to include the <code class=\"inline\">FooBar</code> class file. The autoloader implementation is pretty simple in the above example, but you could build on this by registering multiple autoloaders for different kinds of classes.</p><p>In practice, you won't often be writing your own autoloader, though. That's what Composer is for! In the next section, we’ll discuss how to use Composer for autoloading in PHP.</p><h2>How Autoloading Works With Composer<br>\n</h2><p>Firstly, make sure to <a href=\"https://code.tutsplus.com/tutorials/what-is-composer-for-php-and-how-to-install-it--cms-35160\" target=\"_self\">install Composer on your system</a> if you want to follow along with the examples. When it comes to autoloading with Composer, there are different methods you could choose from.</p><ul class=\"roundup-block__contents posts--half-width roundup-block--list\"><li class=\"roundup-block__content\"><a class=\"roundup-block__content-link\" href=\"https://code.tutsplus.com/tutorials/what-is-composer-for-php-and-how-to-install-it--cms-35160\"><img class=\"roundup-block__preview-image\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/769/posts/35160/preview_image/web%20dev.jpg\"><div class=\"roundup-block__primary-category topic-code\">PHP</div>\n<div class=\"roundup-block__content-title\">What Is Composer for PHP and How to Install It</div>\n<div class=\"roundup-block__author\">Sajal Soni</div></a></li></ul><p>Specifically, Composer provides four different methods for autoloading files:</p><ol>\n<li>file autoloading</li>\n<li>classmap autoloading</li>\n<li>PSR-0 autoloading</li>\n<li>PSR-4 autoloading<br>\n</li>\n</ol><p>As per the official Composer documentation, PSR-4 is the recommended way of autoloading, and we’ll go through that in detail in the next section. In this section, we’ll briefly discuss the other three options.</p><p>Before we go ahead, let’s quickly go through the steps that you need to perform when you want to use Composer autoloading.</p><ul>\n<li>Define the <strong>composer.json</strong> file in the root of your project or library. It should contain  directives based on the type of autoloading.</li>\n<li>Run the <code class=\"inline\">composer dump-autoload</code> command to generate the necessary files that Composer will use for autoloading.<br>\n</li>\n<li>Include the <code class=\"inline\">require 'vendor/autoload.php'</code> statement at the top of the file where you want to use autoloading.<br>\n</li>\n</ul><h3>Autoloading: The <code class=\"inline\">files</code> Directive<br>\n</h3><p>File autoloading works similarly to <code class=\"inline\">include</code> or <code class=\"inline\">require</code> statements that allow you to load entire source files. All the source files that are referenced with the <code class=\"inline\">files</code> directive will be loaded every time your application runs. This is useful for loading source files that do not use classes.</p><p>To use file autoloading, provide a list of files in the <code class=\"inline\">files</code> directive of the <strong>composer.json</strong> file, as shown in the following snippet.</p><pre class=\"brush: javascript noskimlinks noskimwords\">{\n    \"autoload\": {\n        \"files\": [\"lib/Foo.php\", \"lib/Bar.php\"]\n    }\n}</pre><p>As you can see, we can provide a list of files in the <code class=\"inline\">files</code> directive that we want to autoload with Composer. After you create the <strong>composer.json</strong> file in your project root with the above contents, you just need to run the <code class=\"inline\">composer dump-autoload</code> command to create the necessary autoloader files. These will be created under the <strong>vendor</strong> directory. Finally, you need to include the <code class=\"inline\">require 'vendor/autoload.php'</code> statement at the top of the file where you want to autoload files with Composer, as shown in the following snippet.</p><pre class=\"brush: php noskimlinks noskimwords\">&lt;?php\nrequire 'vendor/autoload.php';\n \n// code which uses things declared in the \"lib/Foo.php\" or \"lib/Bar.php\" file\n?&gt;</pre><p>The <code class=\"inline\">require 'vendor/autoload.php'</code> statement makes sure that the necessary files are loaded dynamically. <br></p><h3>Autoloading: The <code class=\"inline\">classmap</code> Directive<br>\n</h3><p>Classmap autoloading is an improved version of file autoloading. You just need to provide a list of directories, and Composer will scan all the files in those directories. For each file, Composer will make a list of classes that are contained in that file, and whenever one of those classes is needed, Composer will autoload the corresponding file.</p><p>Let’s quickly revise the <strong>composer.json</strong> file to demonstrate the classmap autoloader.</p><pre class=\"brush: javascript noskimlinks noskimwords\">{\n    \"autoload\": {\n        \"classmap\": [\"lib\"]\n    }\n}</pre><p>Run the <code class=\"inline\">composer dump-autoload</code> command, and Composer will read the files in the <strong>lib</strong> directory to create a map of classes that can be autoloaded.</p><h3>Autoloading: PSR-0<br>\n</h3><p>PSR-0 is a standard recommended by the PHP-FIG group for autoloading. In the PSR-0 standard, you must use namespaces to define your libraries. The fully qualified class name must reflect the <code class=\"inline\">\\&lt;Vendor Name&gt;\\(&lt;Namespace&gt;\\)*&lt;Class Name&gt;</code> structure. Also, your classes must be saved in files that follow the same directory structure as that of the namespaces.</p><p>Let’s have a look at the following <code class=\"inline\">composer.json</code> file.</p><pre class=\"brush: javascript noskimlinks noskimwords\">{\n    \"autoload\": {\n        \"psr-0\": {\n            \"Tutsplus\\\\Library\": \"src\"\n        }\n    }\n}</pre><p>In PSR-0 autoloading, you need to map namespaces to directories. In the above example, we’re telling Composer that anything which starts with the <code class=\"inline\">Tutsplus\\Library</code> namespace should be available in the <strong>src\\Tutsplus\\Library</strong> directory.</p><p>For example, if you want to define the <code class=\"inline\">Foo</code> class in the <strong>src\\Tutsplus\\Library</strong> directory, you need to create the <strong>src\\Tutsplus\\Library\\Foo.php</strong> file as shown in the following snippet:</p><pre class=\"brush: php noskimlinks noskimwords\">&lt;?php\nnamespace Tutsplus\\Library;\n\nclass Foo \n{\n    //...\n}\n?&gt;</pre><p>As you can see, this class is defined in the <code class=\"inline\">Tutsplus\\Library</code> namespace. Also, the file name corresponds to the class name. Let’s quickly see how you could autoload the <code class=\"inline\">Foo</code> class.</p><pre class=\"brush: php noskimlinks noskimwords\">&lt;?php\nrequire 'vendor/autoload.php';\n \n$objFoo = new Tutsplus\\Library\\Foo();\n?&gt;</pre><p>Composer will autoload the <code class=\"inline\">Foo</code> class from the <strong>src\\Tutsplus\\Library</strong> directory.</p><p>So that was a brief explanation of file, classmap, and PSR-0 autoloading in Composer. In the next section, we’ll see how PSR-4 autoloading works.</p><h2>How PSR-4 Autoloading Works With Composer<br>\n</h2><p>In the previous section, we discussed how PSR-0 autoloading works. PSR-4 is similar to PSR-0 autoloading in that you need to use namespaces, but you don’t need to mimic the directory structure with namespaces.</p><p>In PSR-0 autoloading, you must map namespaces to the directory structure. As we discussed in the previous section, if you want to autoload the <code class=\"inline\">Tutsplus\\Library\\Foo</code> class, it must be located at <strong>src\\Tutsplus\\Library\\Foo.php</strong>. In PSR-4 autoloading, you can shorten the directory structure, which results in a much simpler directory structure compared to PSR-0 autoloading.</p><p>We’ll revise the example above—see if you can spot the differences.</p><p>Here's what the <strong>composer.json</strong> file looks with PSR-4 autoloading.</p><pre class=\"brush: javascript noskimlinks noskimwords\">{\n    \"autoload\": {\n        \"psr-4\": {\n            \"Tutsplus\\\\Library\\\\\": \"src\"\n        }\n    }\n}</pre><p>It’s important to note that we’ve added trailing backslashes at the end of namespaces. The above mapping tells Composer that anything which starts with the <code class=\"inline\">Tutsplus\\Library</code> namespace should be available in the <strong>src</strong> directory. So you don’t need to create the <strong>Tutsplus</strong> and <strong>Library</strong> directories. For example, if you request the <code class=\"inline\">Tutsplus\\Library\\Foo</code> class, Composer will try to load the <strong>src\\Foo.php</strong> file.</p><p>It’s important to understand that the <code class=\"inline\">Foo</code> class is still defined under the <code class=\"inline\">Tutsplus\\Library</code> namespace; it’s just that you don’t need to create directories that mimic the namespaces. The <strong>src\\Foo.php</strong> file contents will be identical to those of the <strong>src\\Tutsplus\\Library\\Foo.php</strong> file in the<strong> </strong>previous section.</p><p>As you can see, PSR-4 results in a much simpler directory structure, since you can omit creating nested directories while still using full namespaces.</p><p>PSR-4 is the recommended way of autoloading, and it’s widely accepted in the PHP community. You should start using it in your applications if you haven’t done so already!</p><h2>Conclusion<br>\n</h2><p>Today, we discussed autoloading in PHP. Starting with the introduction of different kinds of Composer autoloading techniques, we discussed PSR-0 and PSR-4 autoloading standards in detail in the latter half of the article.</p>\n<h2>Learn PHP With a Free Online Course</h2>\n<p>If you want to learn PHP, check out our <a href=\"https://code.tutsplus.com/courses/php-fundamentals\" target=\"_self\">free online course on PHP fundamentals</a>!</p><figure><div class=\"wistia_responsive_padding\"><div class=\"wistia_responsive_wrapper\"><div class=\"wistia_embed wistia_async_v49six2ywx videoFoam=true\"> </div></div></div></figure><p>In this course, you'll learn the fundamentals of PHP programming. href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/slice-responsive-jquery-slider-and-carousel-plugin/24922153\" target=\"_self\">Slice</a>\n</h3><figure class=\"post_image\"><a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/slice-responsive-jquery-slider-and-carousel-plugin/24922153\" target=\"_self\"><img alt=\"Slice\" framework. </p><p>Do you want to create hybrid apps that work on both Android and iOS? With Ionic, you no longer need to create separate apps for Android and iOS operating systems. Instead, with Ionic, you can create one code base that is compatible with both Android and iOS. </p><p>One great benefit of using Ionic is that you don't need to learn a new language from scratch. It is used to generate Ionic Framework code for apps. With it, you can create no-limit apps, complete with a back-end. </p><p>The code you generate is based on your instructions and on your brand. The generated TypeScript, PHP, HTML, and SCSS code can then be edited again for complete customization.</p><p>IMABuildeRz V3 comes with add-ons that allow you to create apps with or without coding skills.</p><h3>13. <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/ionic-3-ready-to-use-elements-with-12-categories/25275815\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Ionic 3 Ready-to-Use Elements with 12+ Categories</a> <br>\n</h3><p>This <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/ionic-3-ready-to-use-elements-with-12-categories/25275815\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Ionic theme</a> will help you get started quickly with almost any kind of app that you plan to create using Ionic.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/ionic-3-ready-to-use-elements-with-12-categories/25275815\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"Ionic Opus UI Kit\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1251/posts/34763/image/ionic_3_opus_components.png\" class=\"loaded\"></a></figure><p>Instead of a single app dedicated to creating something specific like food delivery, restaurant, or dating applications, this Ionic theme comes with different individual components that you can use in your own apps.</p><p>There are currently 12 different components to display chats, addresses, profile, home feed, and orders, as well as login and registration. Each of these components has multiple variants for the UI. For example, there are five different UI demos for the grid component. You can pick the one that meets your needs and easily integrate it in your application.</p><p>The UI looks great for each component, and the code has been optimized to give you the best possible performance, without any lag.</p><h2>Free Ionic App Templates and Components<br>\n</h2><p>It is not always possible to find completely developed Ionic app templates for free. Most of the time, you can expect to get individual components for free, like login screens or custom lists. Here are a few free Ionic app components and templates for you to explore.</p><h3>Ionic 4 Custom Color Picker</h3><p>This component will help you quickly add a <a href=\"https://market.ionicframework.com/themes/custome-color-picker\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">custom color picker</a> to your Ionic app. Instructions for installation and usage are given on the download page.</p><h3>Ionic 4 Starter Theme</h3><p>This is a basic <a href=\"https://market.ionicframework.com/themes/ionic4-start-theme\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Ionic 4 starter theme</a> with several pages like login, register, about, and edit profile. It also contains a couple of components like notifications and a popup menu.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Ionic 4 Start Theme\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1251/posts/34763/image/ionic4_free_start_theme.png\" class=\"loaded\"></figure><h3>Beautiful Custom List</h3><p>This <a href=\"https://market.ionicframework.com/themes/beautiful-custom-list\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">beautiful custom list</a> is actually a standalone component that you can integrate in your other Ionic apps. As the name suggests, it is simply a list of different items. However, the UI is very appealing.</p><h3>Ionic 3 Multi Purpose Theme</h3><p>This is yet another basic <a href=\"https://market.ionicframework.com/themes/ionic-3-multi-purpose-theme\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Ionic 3 theme</a> that gives you access to common ready-made components and pages. You will get things like a welcome page, a news feed page, and a sidebar with sliding animation.</p><h2>Tips on Getting Started With an Ionic App</h2><p>Even though Ionic makes it a lot easier for people to quickly create apps for both Android and iOS, it can still be a bit challenging for absolute beginners. There are a couple of things that you can do to get started quickly.</p><h3>1. Read the Documentation</h3><p>The best way to learn about Ionic and get help when you are stuck is to read <a href=\"https://ionicframework.com/docs/\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">the documentation</a>. It provides information about a variety of topics like installation, theming, components, and native APIs.<br></p><h3>2. Try Creating Basic Apps</h3><p>The next step in the right direction would be for you to try to create some basic apps of your own. This could be something simple like a timer or calendar app in the beginning. After that, take a look at free apps created by other users and see the process they followed.</p><h3>3. Start Developing Complete Apps</h3><p>Once you fully understand the basic concepts and have created a few basic apps, it's time to start working on the app you wanted to create in the first place.</p><h2>Build Your Ionic App Now! </h2><p>A fully completed app will have a lot of components, screens, and functionality that will take a lot of time and effort on your part to create from scratch. The Ionic apps and templates <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/tags/ionic?sort=price-asc&amp;term=ionic&amp;view=grid#content\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">available on CodeCanyon</a> will prove a great time-saver for you at this point.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/tags/ionic?sort=sales&amp;term=ionic&amp;view=grid#content\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"Ionic Apps on Codecanyon\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1251/posts/34763/image/ionic_codecanyon_bottom.png\" class=\"loaded\"></a></figure><h2>Take Advantage of Ionic Tutorials From Envato Tuts+</h2><p>If you want to improve your skills in building Ionic apps and templates, then check out some of the ever-so-useful <a href=\"https://code.tutsplus.com/categories/ionic\">Ionic tutorials</a> we have on offer!</p><ul class=\"roundup-block__contents posts--half-width roundup-block--card\">\n<li class=\"roundup-block__content posts__post\"><article><header><a class=\"posts__post-preview\" href=\"https://code.tutsplus.com/articles/how-to-learn-ionic-start-with-these-courses-and-tutorials--cms-33989\"><img class=\"posts__post-preview-image posts__post-preview-image--regular\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/769/posts/33989/preview_image/mobile%20learning%20guide.jpg\"></a><a class=\"roundup-block__content-link posts__post-title\" href=\"https://code.tutsplus.com/articles/how-to-learn-ionic-start-with-these-courses-and-tutorials--cms-33989\"><h1 class=\"nolinks\">How to Learn Ionic: Start With These Courses and Tutorials</h1></a></header><div class=\"posts__post-teaser\">New to Ionic? 22:02:03","updatedTime":"2020-08-19 22:02:03","title":"Parse XML to an Array in PHP With SimpleXML","link":"https://code.tutsplus.com/tutorials/parse-xml-to-an-array-in-php-with-simplexml--cms-35529","description":"<p>In this post, you'll learn how to parse XML into an array in PHP. SimpleXML is a PHP extension that makes this possible.</p><p>In your day-to-day PHP development, sometimes you'll need to deal with XML content. Whether it’s exporting data as XML documents or processing incoming XML documents in your application, it’s always handy to have a library that can perform these operations smoothly. When it comes to dealing with XML in PHP, there are different methods to choose from. In fact, there are different extensions available in PHP that allow you to read and parse XML documents.<br></p><p>PHP’s XML parser is based on James Clark’s expat library, which is a stream-oriented XML library written in C. This XML parser library allows you to parse XML documents, but it’s not able to validate them. It’s event-based and stream-oriented, and thus it’s really useful when you’re dealing with very large XML files—but a little more complicated than it needs to be for small files. <br></p><p>The other option is the SimpleXML extension, which is one of the most popular extensions used by the PHP community to process XML documents. The SimpleXML extension allows you to parse XML documents very easily, just as if you were reading a file in PHP.</p><p>In this article, we’re going to use the SimpleXML extension to demonstrate how you could convert XML content into an array. If you want to follow along with the example in this article, make sure that you’ve installed the SimpleXML extension in your PHP installation.</p><h2>The SimpleXML PHP Extension<br>\n</h2><p>The SimpleXML PHP extension provides a complete toolset which you can use to read, write and parse XML documents in your PHP applications. It’s important to note that the SimpleXML extension requires PHP 5 at a minimum. Also, it requires the libxml PHP extension.</p><p>The SimpleXML extension is enabled by default, but if you want to check if it's enabled in your PHP installation, you can check it quickly by using the <code class=\"inline\">phpinfo()</code> function.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"The phpinfo Function\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/413/posts/35529/image/how-to-convert-xml-to-array-in-php-with-simplexml-phpinfo.png\"></figure><p>As you can see, you should see the SimpleXML section in the output of the <code class=\"inline\">phpinfo()</code> function.</p><p>The SimpleXML extension provides different functions that you could use to read and parse XML content.</p><h4>Loading an XML String or File With SimpleXML</h4><p>For example, if you want to parse the XML file, you can use the <code class=\"inline\">simplexml_load_file()</code> function. The <code class=\"inline\">simplexml_load_file()</code> function allows you to read and parse the XML file in a single call. On the other hand, if you have an XML string which you want to convert into an XML document object, you can use the <code class=\"inline\">simplexml_load_string()</code> function.</p><p>You could also use the <code class=\"inline\">file_get_contents()</code> function to read the file contents and pass the resulting string to the <code class=\"inline\">simplexml_load_string()</code> function, which eventually parses it into an object. Alternatively, if you prefer the object-oriented way, you could also use the <code class=\"inline\">SimpleXMLElement</code> class and its utility methods to convert an XML string into an object.</p><p>In this article, we’re going to use the <code class=\"inline\">simplexml_load_file()</code> function to read an XML file, and we’ll see how to convert it into an array. Next, we’ll go through a real-world example to demonstrate how to do this.</p><h2>How to Convert XML to an Array With PHP</h2><p>In this section, we’ll see how you can convert XML content into an array.</p><p>First of all, let’s quickly go through the steps that you need to follow to convert XML content into an array with the help of the SimpleXML extension.</p><ul>\n<li>Read the file contents and parse them. At the end of this step, the content is parsed and converted into the <code class=\"inline\">SimpleXMLElement</code> object format. We’re going to use the <code class=\"inline\">simplexml_load_file()</code> function to achieve this.</li>\n<li>Next, you need to convert the <code class=\"inline\">SimpleXMLElement</code> object into a JSON representation by using the <code class=\"inline\">json_encode()</code> function.<br>\n</li>\n<li>Finally, you need to use the <code class=\"inline\">json_decode()</code> function to decode the JSON content so that it eventually generates an array of all documents.<br>\n</li>\n</ul><p>For demonstration purposes, let’s assume that we have an XML file as shown in the following snippet. We’ll call it <strong>employees.xml</strong>. It contains the basic details of all employees. Our aim is to convert it into an array that you could use for further processing.</p><pre class=\"brush: xml noskimlinks noskimwords\">&lt;?xml version='1.0'?&gt;   \n&lt;employees&gt;   \n    &lt;employee id=\"1\"&gt;\n        &lt;name&gt;John&lt;/name&gt;   \n        &lt;email&gt;john@example.com&lt;/email&gt;\n        &lt;address&gt;\n           &lt;street&gt;3201  Glendale Avenue&lt;/street&gt;\n           &lt;city&gt;Los Angeles&lt;/city&gt;\n           &lt;state&gt;CA&lt;/state&gt;\n        &lt;/address&gt;\n    &lt;/employee&gt;\n    &lt;employee id=\"2\"&gt;\n        &lt;name&gt;Mike&lt;/name&gt;\n        &lt;email&gt;mike@example.com&lt;/email&gt;\n        &lt;address&gt;\n           &lt;street&gt;781  Stroop Hill Road&lt;/street&gt;\n           &lt;city&gt;Duluth&lt;/city&gt;\n           &lt;state&gt;GA&lt;/state&gt;\n        &lt;/address&gt;\n    &lt;/employee&gt;\n&lt;/employees&gt;</pre><p>As you can see, the <strong>employees.xml</strong> file contains the names and emails of employees. It’s important to note that the <code class=\"inline\">employee-id</code> value is passed as an attribute of the <code class=\"inline\">&lt;employee&gt;</code> tag.</p><p>Next, create the <strong>simplexml.php</strong> file with the following contents.</p><pre class=\"brush: php noskimlinks noskimwords\">&lt;?php\nlibxml_use_internal_errors(TRUE);\n\n$objXmlDocument = simplexml_load_file(\"employees.xml\");\n\nif ($objXmlDocument === FALSE) {\n    echo \"There were errors parsing the XML file.\\n\";\n    foreach(libxml_get_errors() as $error) {\n        echo $error-&gt;message;\n    }\n    exit;\n}\n\n$objJsonDocument = json_encode($objXmlDocument);\n$arrOutput = json_decode($objJsonDocument, TRUE);\n\necho \"&lt;pre&gt;\";\nprint_r($arrOutput);\n?&gt;</pre><p>Let’s go through the important snippets in the above example to understand how it works.<br></p><h3>Read and Parse the XML File<br>\n</h3><p>Firstly, we’ve used the <code class=\"inline\">libxml_use_internal_errors()</code> function to disable standard libxml errors and enable user error handling. In this way, we can catch the XML errors during parsing and display them in a user-friendly way. This is also really useful in the development phase.<br></p><p>Next, we’ve used the <code class=\"inline\">simplexml_load_file()</code> function to read and parse the <strong>employees.xml</strong> file. The first argument of the <code class=\"inline\">simplexml_load_file()</code> function is a path to the XML file. It’s important to note that you need to adjust this path as needed. In the above example, it’s assumed that the <strong>employees.xml</strong> file is at the same directory level as that of the <strong>simplexml.php</strong> file. If the XML file is parsed successfully, it returns an object of the <code class=\"inline\">SimpleXMLElement</code> class; otherwise, it returns <code class=\"inline\">FALSE</code>.</p><p>Next, if the <code class=\"inline\">$objXmlDocument</code> variable is set to <code class=\"inline\">FALSE</code>, there was a problem parsing the <strong>employees.xml</strong> file. In that case, we use the <code class=\"inline\">libxml_get_errors()</code> function to get all the errors and display them for debugging purposes. The <code class=\"inline\">$objXmlDocument</code> variable is set to <code class=\"inline\">TRUE</code> if the <strong>employees.xml</strong> file is parsed successfully.</p><h3>Convert the <code class=\"inline\">SimpleXMLElement</code> Object Into Its JSON Representation<br>\n</h3><p>Next, we’ve used the <code class=\"inline\">json_encode()</code> function to convert the <code class=\"inline\">SimpleXMLElement</code> object into its JSON representation. We’ve stored the JSON string in the <code class=\"inline\">$objJsonDocument</code> variable, as shown in the following snippet.</p><pre class=\"brush: php noskimlinks noskimwords\">$objJsonDocument = json_encode($objXmlDocument);</pre><h3>Decode the JSON String Into an Array<br>\n</h3><p>Finally, we’ve used the <code class=\"inline\">json_decode()</code> function to decode the JSON string data. It’s important to note that we’ve passed <code class=\"inline\">TRUE</code> in the second argument of the <code class=\"inline\">json_decode()</code> function, which converts all objects into associative arrays.</p><pre class=\"brush: php noskimlinks noskimwords\">$arrOutput = json_decode($objJsonDocument, TRUE);</pre><p>Had you not passed <code class=\"inline\">TRUE</code> in the second argument, the <code class=\"inline\">json_decode</code> function would have produced objects of type <code class=\"inline\">StdClass</code> instead of arrays.</p><p>So that's an outline of the whole process. Let’s run the <strong>simplexml.php</strong> file, and you should see the following output.</p><pre class=\"brush: plain noskimlinks noskimwords\">Array\n(\n    [employee] =&gt; Array\n        (\n            [0] =&gt; Array\n                (\n                    [@attributes] =&gt; Array\n                        (\n                            [id] =&gt; 1\n                        )\n                    [name] =&gt; John\n                    [email] =&gt; john@example.com\n                    [address] =&gt; Array\n                        (\n                            [street] =&gt; 3201  Glendale Avenue\n                            [city] =&gt; Los Angeles\n                            [state] =&gt; CA\n                        )\n                )\n\n            [1] =&gt; Array\n                (\n                    [@attributes] =&gt; Array\n                        (\n                            [id] =&gt; 2\n                        )\n                    [name] =&gt; Mike\n                    [email] =&gt; mike@example.com\n                    [address] =&gt; Array\n                        (\n                            [street] =&gt; 781  Stroop Hill Road\n                            [city] =&gt; Duluth\n                            [state] =&gt; GA\n                        )\n                )\n        )\n)</pre><p>As expected, the array contains all the documents. As you may have noticed, it has also parsed the <code class=\"inline\">id</code> field, which is attached with each document in the form of an attribute, and you can access it with the <code class=\"inline\">@attributes</code> key, as shown in the above output. Basically, everything is available in the form of key-value pairs. So you have a complete array at your disposal for further processing.</p><p>So that’s how you can convert XML content into an array in PHP. It was a very simple example, but it should give you some insight into the whole process.</p><h2>Conclusion<br>\n</h2><p>In this article, we discussed how to convert an XML file into an array using PHP and SimpleXML. The SimpleXML extension is really useful when it comes to parsing and manipulating XML documents.  <br></p>\n\n\n<h2>The Best PHP Scripts on CodeCanyon</h2>\n \n\n\n<p>The free libraries on Packagist 22:02:03","updatedTime":"2020-08-19 22:02:03","title":"Real-Time Stock Market Data With the marketstack API","link":"https://code.tutsplus.com/tutorials/real-time-stock-market-data-with-marketstack-api--cms-35539","description":"<p>To make sound financial decisions, you need a reliable, up-to-the-minute source of real-time stock market data.&nbsp;</p><p>You want the same source of data used by Microsoft, Amazon, Credit Suisse, and Uber.</p><p>The good news is you don't have to be a major player to have this data in real time.&nbsp;</p><p>Whether you're an individual, small business, financial advisor, or developer, the marketstack API gives you access to real-time, intraday, and historical stock data from 72 global stock exchanges, including Nasdaq, the New York Stock Exchange, and the London Stock Exchange.&nbsp;</p><p>You too can now deliver real-time, intraday, historical stock, or end-of-day market data to your website and to your clients and create satisfying user experiences.&nbsp;<br></p><p>It's simple and cost-effective: let me introduce you to marketstack.&nbsp;<br></p><h2>What Is the marketstack API?</h2><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"marketstack API\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1997/posts/35539/image/4E6C2655-368C-4BA6-AA8E-75E0E1AB7F64.jpeg\"></figure><p>marketstack is a popular, easy-to-use REST API interface that delivers real-time, intraday, and historical stock market data. &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</p><p>The API is powered by cutting-edge technology and a scalable cloud infrastructure capable of handling several million API requests per hour with ease.&nbsp;<br></p><p>You can search from 125,000+ worldwide stock tickers, collected from 72 global exchanges, including Nasdaq and the NYSE.</p><p>Using the marketstack REST API, you will be able to obtain end-of-day and intraday data, as well as historical market data for the last 30 years.</p><p>With the marketstack API, you can:</p><ul><li>query for&nbsp;real-time, intraday, and historical stock market data</li><li>define multiple stock symbols</li><li>retrieve extensive data from about 72+ stock exchanges</li><li>access 125,000+ stock tickers from more than 50 countries</li><li>retrieve information on time zones, currencies, and more</li></ul><h2>Why Use the marketstack API?</h2><h4>It Uses JSON</h4><p>marketstack uses the lightweight JSON format, and HTTP GET for all the requests. API queries are easy to create and to interpret.<br></p><h4>Integration With Multiple Languages</h4><p>The API integrates with widely used programming languages and platforms: PHP, Python, jQuery, Node, Go, and Ruby. &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;</p><h4>Scalable</h4><p>The marketstack API can scale with your information and data demands. It can easily handle spikes and increases in&nbsp;your daily queries.&nbsp;</p><h4>Bank-Grade Security</h4><p>Client data is protected by a layer of heavy security. Each bit and byte sent to and from the marketstack API is encrypted using industry-standard 256-bit HTTPS encryption.</p><h4>Reliable Information Sources&nbsp;</h4><p>Stock market data provided by the marketstack API is licensed and sourced from multiple high-authority market data providers around the world.&nbsp;</p><h4>Proof in Numbers&nbsp;</h4><p>Trusted by 30,000 companies and 75 universities.&nbsp;</p><h4>Documentation</h4><p>The marketstack API comes with extensive and detailed documentation.&nbsp;</p><h2>How It Works</h2><p>The marketstack API is built upon a RESTful and easy-to-understand request and response structure.&nbsp;</p><ol><li>API requests are always sent in the URL string with a series of required and optional HTTP GET parameters.</li><li>API responses are provided in lightweight JSON format.</li></ol><h2>Quick Tutorial<br></h2><p>Here is an example of the information returned from a marketstack API query.</p><p><img alt=\"marketstack API query result\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1997/posts/35539/image/BB2F29CD-A87D-45B7-ABCE-AEFE7EA5A626.jpeg\"><br></p><p>It's very easy to get set up and start using marketstack. This short tutorial will show you how.&nbsp;</p><p>To get started, first sign up for a free account at&nbsp;<a href=\"https://marketstack.com/signup\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">marketstack</a>. Once you've registered, you'll be taken to the <a href=\"https://marketstack.com/quickstart\" target=\"_self\">marketstack API quick start screen</a>. From here, you can get your API key and try some example API queries.&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"API endpoints\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1997/posts/35539/image/BE46B661-D87D-4A9F-953E-481D66065042.jpeg\"></figure><p>Now you can perform a request. Using your API key and the example queries shown in the quick start guide, you can look up stock prices and other information. For example, let's perform a single request for Apple stock.</p><p>The quick start guide shows the following format for the query.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Make API Request format\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1997/posts/35539/image/E21F455C-5086-4853-957F-546ECCD7BC57.jpeg\"></figure><p>Click the example to try the request, or enter it into your address bar:</p><p><a href=\"https://api.marketstack.com/v1/eod?access_key=YOUR_ACCESS_KEY&amp;symbols=AAPL\"><strong>http://api.marketstack.com/v1/eod?access_key=YOUR_ACCESS_KEY&amp;symbols=AAPL</strong></a>&nbsp;</p><p>Be sure to copy your access key into this URL to try it. If your API request was successful, the marketstack API will return <code>pagination</code>&nbsp;information as well as a&nbsp;<code>data</code>&nbsp;object, which contains a separate sub-object for each requested date/time and symbol.&nbsp;<br></p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"pagination information and data object\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1997/posts/35539/image/85B5796B-3AC4-4D31-A690-998C236B1039.jpeg\"></figure><p>Note that requests you make on the free plan are not encrypted, so you must use the HTTP protocol for free requests. If you try to use HTTPS, you will get the message that \"<strong>Your current subscription plan does not support HTTPS encryption</strong>\". If HTTPS is important to you, then you'll need to go with a paid plan.</p><p>You can learn more from the&nbsp;<a href=\"https://marketstack.com/documentation\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">official marketstack documentation</a>, including code examples for JavaScript, PHP, Python, and more.&nbsp;</p><h2>Pricing<br></h2><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"marketstack subscription options\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1997/posts/35539/image/9F4D714A-A63A-4394-8479-0048BF3A3E15.jpeg\"></figure><p>marketstack has several market data subscription plans.&nbsp;</p><p><strong>Free:&nbsp;</strong>You get&nbsp;1,000 data requests per month&nbsp;without paying anything. This applies for all&nbsp;supported stock tickers and exchanges. It does not offer&nbsp;intraday data, and you are restricted to one year of historical data. No credit card is needed to register.&nbsp;</p><p>Who is this plan best for? It's&nbsp;best for&nbsp;beginners&nbsp;wanting to test the waters and see how marketstack works.&nbsp;</p><p><b>Basic:</b>&nbsp;gets you 10,000 requests per month, support for intraday data, access to ten-year historical data, HTTPS encryption, a commercial license, and more. At the time of writing, this plan is $9.99 per month, or $7.99 if billed yearly.&nbsp;</p><p>Who is this plan best for? For those who have seen how marketstack works and&nbsp;want to get serious using it.&nbsp;</p><p><strong>Professional (Most Popular)</strong>: With this plan, you get&nbsp;real-time updates, full historical data, up to 100,000 requests per month, and technical support.&nbsp;</p><p><strong>Business</strong>: This plan gives you all the tools you will ever need, for up to 500,000 monthly requests, real-time updates, and direct support. &nbsp;</p><p><b>Enterprise</b>: If none of the other plans are adequate, you can get&nbsp;custom pricing that is tailored to&nbsp;your needs.&nbsp;<br></p><h2>Conclusion</h2><p>marketstack is trusted by 30,000 companies and 75 universities. This is a big mark of approval. The interfaces for requests and responses are easy to use, and there is detailed documentation that explains all the API parameters.</p><p><a href=\"https://marketstack.com/\" target=\"_self\">Try it out today with a free API key!</a></p><div class=\"mediafed_ad\"><img border=\"0\" height=\"1\" src=\"http://audio.tutsplus.com.feedsportal.com/c/35227/f/668806/s/35539/sc/4/mf.gif\" width=\"1\" /><a
