topic-code\" href=\"https://code.tutsplus.com/categories/wordpress\">WordPress</a></div></footer></article></li>\n</ul><h2>4 Tips for Creating a Successful Membership Website </h2><p>Choosing a professional, feature-packed membership plugin is the first step to creating a successful membership website, but there’s still lots you can do to help grow your audience.</p><p>In this final section, I’ll share four ways that you can encourage people to sign up, engage with your community features, and ultimately renew their membership, so you generate the maximum revenue from your WordPress community website. </p><h3>1. Offer a Free Trial</h3><p>Free trials are one of the most effective ways to market <em>anything</em>—and membership websites are no exception. </p><p>Customers like to know exactly what they’re getting before they make a purchase. Giving potential new subscribers a way to experience all of your website’s great membership features, first-hand and for free, can encourage them to make a purchase.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/armember-complete-wordpress-membership-system/17785056\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"ARMember Best Membership Plugin For WordPress With Free Trial\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/2660/posts/35597/image/ARMember-membership-plugin.jpg\"></a><figcaption><a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/armember-complete-wordpress-membership-system/17785056\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">ARMember</a> is a WordPress membership management plugin that let's visitors choose a free trial. </figcaption></figure><h3>2. Create Multiple Subscription Levels</h3><p>To get the maximum number of registrations, your membership plans need to appeal to a wide audience. </p><p>Unless you have a specific reason not to, it’s always a good idea to create multiple membership levels—for example, you might offer Bronze, Silver, and Gold subscriptions, or Monthly and Annual plans. For the best results, each membership should offer unique perks, and there should be a considerable difference in pricing.</p><p>If you’re trying to monetize your website, then multiple membership levels can also be a way to increase the average spend per member. If a new customer expresses an interest in a Silver subscription, then you have the opportunity to upsell them a Gold subscription.</p><p>Even after a user has purchased their subscription, there may still be upsell opportunities in the future. In these scenarios, it can often help to present the upsell as an exclusive bonus—for example, if a subscriber's Silver membership is about to expire, then you could offer them a Gold membership at a discounted rate, as a special thank you for being such a loyal customer. </p><h3>3. Keep in Constant Communication With Your Community </h3><p>Today’s typical Internet user has a short attention span, so even after someone purchases a subscription, you’ll need to work hard to keep them engaged with your website.</p><p>Most premium WordPress plugins have features that are designed to help you hold your audience’s attention—for example, both <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/armember-complete-wordpress-membership-system/17785056\">ARMember</a> and <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/youzer-new-wordpress-user-profiles-era/19716647\">Youzer</a> integrate with popular email marketing solutions Mailchimp and Mailster. You can encourage members to visit your website by sending them regular newsletters and email updates about all the new and exciting content they’re missing out on.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/youzer-new-wordpress-user-profiles-era/19716647\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"Youzer Best Membership Plugin for WordPress\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/2660/posts/35597/image/Youzer-best-membership-plugins-wordpress.jpg\"></a><figcaption>Build and talk with your online community with the <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/youzer-new-wordpress-user-profiles-era/19716647\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Youzer WordPress membership plugin</a>.</figcaption></figure><p>Other plugins, such as <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/woocommerce-membership/8746370\">WooCommerce Membership</a> and <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/ultimate-learning-pro-wordpress-plugin/21772657\">Ultimate Learning Pro</a>, allow you to “drip” content to your users. By carefully scheduling content in advance, you can ensure that <em>something</em> is always happening on your website, which will encourage members to get into the habit of regularly checking your site, in the hopes of discovering new content.</p><h3>4. Create a Sense of Community</h3><p>A successful online community needs to <em>feel</em> like a community, so you should try to give subscribers multiple ways to connect with one another.</p><p>As a minimum, visitors should be able to comment on your content and reply to comments left by other members, but you could also allow users to post their own content; view other people’s profiles; create and join groups, and exchange instant messages with other members of the community. </p><p>Many premium WordPress plugins also include features that are inspired by social media—for example, <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/userpro-user-profiles-with-social-login/5958681?_ga=2.209361236.71199192.1575379090-1280144257.1574810364\">UserPro</a> allows members to “follow” each other and view logs of every member’s recent activity, including any new content or comments that this person has posted.  </p><figure class=\"post_image\"><a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/userpro-user-profiles-with-social-login/5958681\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\"><img alt=\"UserPro Member List Plugin\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/2660/posts/35597/image/userpro-socials-userpro-user-profiles-with-social-login-5958681.jpg\"></a><figcaption><a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/userpro-user-profiles-with-social-login/5958681\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">UserPro</a> lets members of your site connect with each other in meaningful ways.</figcaption></figure><p>By fostering a sense of community, you can encourage members to build an emotional connection to this community, and by extension your website. </p><h2>More WordPress Plugins For Great Websites From Envato Tuts+</h2><p>You now know that plugins can help you create a WordPress membership site. But there are thousands of plugins that can help you take your website to the next level. If you want to keep improving your website's design and performance, check out some of these selections we've gathered on Envato Tuts+.</p><p><br></p><ul class=\"roundup-block__contents The sizing and spacing options for the layout are very flexible and you have full control over the vertical and horizontal space between different elements.</p><p>The plugin can showcase images in the JPG, PNG or GIF format. It can show videos from YouTube, Vimeo, Dailymotion and Metacafe. You can even add audio clips from websites like SoundCloud,  Mixcloud or Beatport to your portfolio.</p><p>The plugin supports all major browsers and you can easily import or export different settings to get up and running quickly.<br></p><h2>WordPress Flipbook Galleries</h2><h3>10. <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/interactive-3d-flipbook-powered-physics-engine-wordpress-plugin/19389832\">WordPress Flipbook</a>\n</h3><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"WordPress Flipbook\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/456/posts/32638/image/5WordPressFlipbook.JPG\" class=\"loaded\"></figure><p>Revolutionize online books with this <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/interactive-3d-flipbook-powered-physics-engine-wordpress-plugin/19389832\" target=\"_self\">3D WordPress book theme</a>. You can easily use this plugin to create a standard flipbook. Or, using CSS layers, you can insert content like video, audio, hover and navigation effects, HTML, and JavaScript directly into your book to create an interactive experience for your viewers. </p><p>Choose from fully customizable skin options to display your content in a realistic 3D flipbook, complete with page-depth simulation and user-friendly interactive flexible page corners. Pages render in the background, ensuring a smooth reading experience, and smart pans automatically display your flipbook in the most comfortable orientation for reading in any device.</p><p>User MichaelNickel says:</p><blockquote>“This is a truly amazing flipbook plugin, easy to use, with great value for the money! Highly recommended.”<br>\n</blockquote><h3>11. <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/real3d-flipbook-wordpress-plugin/6942587\">Real3D Flipbook</a>\n</h3><figure><div class=\"wistia_responsive_padding\"><div class=\"wistia_responsive_wrapper\"><div class=\"wistia_embed wistia_async_n0tmhwy76f videoFoam=true\"> </div></div></div></figure><p>Create 3D flipbooks to display directly on your website using the Real3D WordPress gallery plugin. Ultra-realistic features like page bending, shiny pages, lights and shadows are available to you—<a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/real3d-flipbook-wordpress-plugin/6942587\" target=\"_self\">just upload your PDF or images and copy and paste the shortcode</a>. </p><p>With automatic fallbacks that ensure your flipbook will display correctly on all platforms, this plugin comes with all the basic and premium features you need: interactive pages, lightbox, single or double page view, and more are all included in this package. Real3D flipbook supports unlimited books and pages and ensures smooth loading by rendering pages one by one, so visitors can start reading instantly.</p><p>User rubikmm says:</p><blockquote>“The plugin is great, very easy to use, very powerful to customize, and the support stands at same level. Keep up the good work.”</blockquote><h3>12. <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/diamond-flipbook-jquerypluginwordpress/5823062\">Diamond Flipbook</a>\n</h3><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Diamond Flipbook Plugin\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/456/posts/32638/image/10Diamond.jpg\" class=\"loaded\"></figure><p>The Diamond WordPress flipbook plugin allows you to <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/diamond-flipbook-jquerypluginwordpress/5823062\" target=\"_self\">create flipbooks from a variety of source files</a>. Automatically convert PDFs, or upload multiple JPGs at the same time to create a flipbook. You can also manually add pages, or simply enter text directly into the WYSIWYG editor. Then, either add a shortcode for the generated flipbook to your website or post an image link that will launch a lightbox with one click. </p><p>This WordPress gallery plugin also offers YouTube support. Fully responsive and with no Flash needed, this plugin works reliably on both mobile and desktop.</p><p>User josephdelaubriere says:</p><blockquote>“Great plugin and very simple to use.”<br>\n</blockquote><div><br></div><h2>WordPress Grid Galleries</h2><h3>13. <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/the-grid-responsive-wordpress-grid-plugin/13306812\">The Grid</a>\n</h3><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"The Grid gallery plugin\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/456/posts/32638/image/15TheGrid.JPG\" class=\"loaded\"></figure><p>The Grid is a WordPress gallery plugin that allows you to display any post type—think standard, audio, video, social stream, gallery, link, or quote—in a fully customizable grid system. With a powerful admin panel, the possibilities are unlimited with this grid gallery. In this fully responsive plugin, loading speed is optimized by lightweight jQuery script, and a custom cache system boosts your gallery’s performance. </p><p>With built-in lightbox, WooCommerce support, more than 40 animation styles, and one-click import and export, this is truly one of the most advanced WordPress gallery plugins, so try it out—it can be easily integrated with any WordPress theme or custom style.</p><p>User dehlia13300 says:</p><blockquote>“The most flexible grid plugin I have ever used. I absolutely love it! It's  really easy to use and the documentation is very helpful. A must have  for any blog, website, and e-commerce. Highly recommend The Grid for those who want a responsive WordPress plugin that delivers what it promises.”</blockquote><h3>14. <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/smart-grid-gallery-responsive-wordpress-gallery-plugin/8365014\">Smart Grid</a>\n</h3><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Smart Grid gallery plugin\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/456/posts/32638/image/16SmartGrid.JPG\" class=\"loaded\"></figure><p>Turn any WordPress gallery shortcode into a responsive and touch-friendly grid gallery. Full of customization options, this plugin allows you to create dynamic image grids with lightboxes, CSS2 animations, and YouTube and Vimeo support. Simply wrap any existing <code class=\"inline\">[gallery]</code> shortcode tag with <code class=\"inline\">[smart-grid]</code> open and close tags to <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/smart-grid-gallery-responsive-wordpress-gallery-plugin/8365014\" target=\"_self\">introduce features like infinite scroll, hover effects, and more to your WordPress g</a><a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/smart-grid-gallery-responsive-wordpress-gallery-plugin/8365014\" target=\"_self\">alleries</a>.</p><p>User rhondagreene says:</p><blockquote>“A great way to dress up the native WordPress gallery! Lots of features and options, and it was easy to incorporate into my existing setup.”</blockquote><h3>15. <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/ubergrid-responsive-grid-builder-for-wordpress/4851992\">UberGrid</a>\n</h3><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"UberGrid gallery plugin\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/456/posts/32638/image/17UberGrid.JPG\" class=\"loaded\"></figure><p>Another grid-based WordPress gallery plugin, <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/ubergrid-responsive-grid-builder-for-wordpress/4851992\" target=\"_self\">UberGrid creates a stylish square-themed gallery</a> using manually added content or automatically loaded content from WordPress. This gallery plugin can be used to display your content to create an attractive display for portfolios, WooCommerce products, photos, blog posts, or other any other content looking for a modern and effective treatment. </p><p>The look of your gallery is highly customizable, and a built-in lightbox has image, Google Maps, YouTube, Vimeo, and text support. Fully responsive and retina ready, with fast CSS3 animations and effects in supported browsers, UberGrid makes all this functionality available to you, with no coding required.</p><p>User tsjemo says:</p><blockquote>“UberGrid is really good, easy to use, and highly customizable.”</blockquote><h2>Miscellaneous WordPress Gallery Plugins</h2><h3>16. <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/multipurpose-before-after-slider/5159016\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Multipurpose Before After Slider</a>\n</h3><p>This Multipurpose Before After slider is not exactly useful for showing dozens of images in a gallery. However, it does provide a cool way of showing the difference between the before and after images of different people and products etc.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Multipurpose Before After Slider\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1251/posts/35499/image/multipurpose-before-after.png\"></figure><p>There are a bunch of examples where this could be used. For example, it could be used on the website of a personal trainer to showcase the physical transformation of different people who joined the fitness class. An interior design company could use it to showcase the before and after versions of a room to building that they renovated.</p><p>You can create as many sliders as you want with this plugin. All the sliders are fully responsive and come with touch and swipe gestures enabled for ease of use on mobile devices. You can also add multiple \"Before\" vs \"After\" image sets in the same slider. Users will be able to navigate through them using buttons available at the bottom.</p><h3>17. <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/photo-contest-wordpress-plugin/8320636\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Photo Contest WordPress Plugin</a>\n</h3><p>This one is actually a WordPress gallery plugin. However, it comes with additional built-in functionality that sets it apart from the rest: it includes a photo contents feature that makes it easy to run photography contests on your website. The entries submitted by different participants are shown in a gallery with one-, two-, three- or four-column layouts.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Photo Contest WordPress Plugin\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1251/posts/35499/image/photo-contest-wordpress-plugin.png\"></figure><p>Users can click on any image to either give it a rating from 1 to 10. You can also set up the contest so that each user has a single vote for their favorite image. And of course you can integrate different social media buttons on the rating page along with 3rd-party commenting plugins.</p><p>The plugin allows you to run multiple contests at the same time. It is also Gutenberg ready and has a responsive design. You have complete control over who can vote for the images. This includes everyone, registered users or selected registered users.</p><p>You can organize the submissions under different categories. All the data about the votes and images can also be exported easily for analysis.</p><p>Try out the <a href=\"https://preview.codecanyon.net/item/photo-contest-wordpress-plugin/full_screen_preview/8320636\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">different demos</a> of the plugin to see if its functionality fits your needs.<br></p><h2>Free WordPress Gallery Plugins</h2><p>In this section, I'll highlight 5 free WordPress gallery plugins. I would like to mention that free plugins usually provide limited functionality compared to premium WordPress gallery plugins from CodeCanyon, but sometimes a free plugin is all you need.</p><h3>1. NextGEN Gallery</h3><p>The <a href=\"https://wordpress.org/plugins/nextgen-gallery/\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">NextGen WordPress gallery plugin</a> provides three main gallery styles called sldieshow, thumbnail and imagebrowser. The admin back-end also has a lot of useful functionality such as batch upload of images, importing metadata and adding, deleting or sorting the images.</p><h3>2. 10Web Photo Gallery</h3><p>The <a href=\"https://wordpress.org/plugins/photo-gallery/\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">10Web Photo Gallery plugin</a> will help you quickly create responsive mobile friendly galleries. It also provides multiple styles for viewing the galleries or individual images. Their is a built-in lightbox and you can create unlimited number of galleries.</p><h3>3. FooGallery Image Gallery</h3><p>The <a href=\"https://wordpress.org/plugins/foogallery/\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">FooGallery plugin</a> makes it very easy for you to add and manage galleries in your WordPress website. It is responsive and supports lazy loading of images.</p><h3>4. Video Gallery—YouTube Gallery</h3><p>This <a href=\"https://wordpress.org/plugins/gallery-videos/\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Video Gallery plugin</a> allows you to quickly add a video gallery to your website. The galleries are fully responsive and touch friendly. It has a built-in lightbox and 9 different layouts.</p><h3>5. Embed Plus for YouTube<br>\n</h3><p>The <a href=\"https://wordpress.org/plugins/youtube-embed-plus/\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Embed Plus WordPress plugin</a> can show videos from a playlist or channel in a gallery based layout on your website. This can be very helpful if you have a YouTube channel that complements the content of your website.</p><h2>Choosing the Best WordPress Gallery Plugin for Your Project</h2><p>As I mentioned earlier, there are over 250 WordPress gallery plugins available on CodeCanyon. It can be a bit difficult to pick one best plugin among them because all of them offer the basic functionality that you require in a gallery plugin.</p><p>In this section, I will recommend some of these plugin that are well suited for some specific use cases.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/video-gallery-wordpress-plugin-w-youtube-vimeo/157782\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Video Gallery WordPress plugin</a> would probably be your best bet if you want to primarily show video content on your website. It offers unmatched features when it comes to showcasing different videos. This includes support for the Vimeo and YouTube API to provide additional functionality. The plugin also supports deep linking and can read <strong>.srt</strong> files to show subtitles on different videos.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/real3d-flipbook-wordpress-plugin/6942587\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Real3D FlipBook WordPress plugin</a> would be a great choice for people who want to recreate the experience of reading a physical book as accurately as possible. The UI looks more polished compared to other plugins and you can add any kind of HTML content over various pages to make them interactive.</p><p>The <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/essential-grid-wordpress-plugin/7563340\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Essential Grid Gallery plugin</a> is ideal for people who want to create a bunch of different gallery layouts using a mix of different types of content such as images, videos and iframes. You just have to choose the source for the gallery content and then selecting a layout and skin. The plugin will take care of everything else. It offers a nice set of animations and the gallery looks great on devices of all screen sizes.<br></p><h2>Conclusion<br>\n</h2><p>There are some WordPress gallery plugins in this roundup that have certainly caught my eye. While some of them excel with CSS3 effects, there were plenty that showed their power on the back-end as well. </p><p>You can find more great WordPress gallery plugins on <a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/search?category=wordpress%2Fgalleries\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">CodeCanyon</a>.</p><p>If you didn't find exactly what you were looking for, perhaps an Envato Tuts+ <a href=\"https://code.tutsplus.com/categories/wordpress\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">WordPress tutorial</a>, <a href=\"https://tutsplus.com/ebooks/search/wordpress\" 22:02:03","updatedTime":"2020-08-19 22:02:03","title":"How to Create a Custom 404 Page With WordPress and Elementor","link":"https://webdesign.tutsplus.com/tutorials/how-to-create-a-custom-404-page-with-wordpress-and-elementor--cms-35555","description":"<p>Spend any amount of time online, and you’ll eventually encounter a 404 page.</p><p>Whether you type a URL incorrectly or click a broken link, a 404 is the Internet’s way of letting you know that the requested page does not exist.</p><p>Even the best website will throw a 404 error from time to time, so why not use this error to your advantage? In this tutorial, I’ll show you how to create a 404 page that helps you connect with your audience, provides a better user experience, and maybe even secures you a few additional sales!&nbsp;</p><p>We’ll be using the Elementor front-end page builder to create three custom 404 pages, using three different methods—and <em>zero</em> code.&nbsp;</p><p>Elementor has over 5 million active installs, but if you’re completely new to Elementor then I’ll also be covering all the background information you need to build professional and compelling websites with Elementor.</p><h2>What We'll Be Covering<br></h2><p>Links don’t live forever!&nbsp;</p><p>Over time, you may need to move or delete certain pages, or decide to merge related posts into a single page that contains all the information your audience could possibly need.&nbsp;</p><p>Whenever the server cannot locate the requested webpage, it’ll display a 404 error. If you don’t add a custom 404 page to your website, then the server will display a stock 404 page—which isn’t exactly the nicest thing to look at.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Every website has a default 404 page but their design often leaves a lot to be desired\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-page-default.png\"></figure><p>In this tutorial, I’ll show you how to replace your website’s default 404 with a custom webpage, using Elementor. Since Elementor is a flexible tool, we’ll be creating a selection of 404 pages, using all of the following methods:&nbsp;</p><ul><li><strong>Create a 404 page using Elementor's Theme Builder</strong>. I'll show you a quick and easy way to create a professionally designed 404 page, using one of Elementor's ready-made templates.</li><li><strong>Design a completely custom 404 page</strong>. Have a specific design in mind? Or want to experiment with a few different potential designs? I'll show you how to build a completely custom 404 page from scratch, by adding text, images, and buttons to a blank template. By the end of this section, you'll have created the following design:</li></ul><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"In this tutorial Ill show you how to turn a blank slate into a custom 404 page\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-complete-custom-404.png\"></figure><ul><li><strong>Envato Elements Template Kits</strong>.&nbsp;Install a themed collection of templates that contain designs for all the pages your website could possibly need—including the following 404 template:</li></ul><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Envato features a wide selection of professionally-designed template kits\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-template-kit-envato.jpg\"></figure><h3>Why Your Website <em>Needs</em> a Custom 404 Page<br></h3><p>Elementor’s user-friendly, drag-and-drop editor may take the pain out of webpage design, but creating a custom 404 page <em>still</em> requires time and effort.</p><p>Before we get stuck into Elementor, let’s look at some of the reasons why you should always consider creating your own 404 page.</p><h4>404 Errors Are Inevitable <br></h4><p>Sometimes, you may need to delete a piece of content, relocate a page to a new URL, or merge multiple posts into a single URL.&nbsp;</p><p>Ideally, you should perform regular content audits where you identify and rectify any broken links, but even if you’re proactive about checking your URLs, some 404 errors are completely out of your control.&nbsp;</p><p>Your website will throw a 404 error if a visitor misspells a URL or a typo-prone third party links to a part of your website that never existed in the first place!&nbsp;While you can’t control other people’s mistakes, you can minimize their impact by creating an engaging 404 page.&nbsp;</p><h4>Connect With Your Audience <br></h4><p>A 404 page is an opportunity to express yourself and strengthen your relationship with your audience.&nbsp;</p><p>Simply type \"best 404 pages\" into Google and you’ll find countless round-ups of creative and unusual 404 pages. Why not follow in their footsteps and use your 404 page as an opportunity to show off your sparkling personality?&nbsp;</p><p>You might treat your visitors to a few 404-related puns, put your own spin on a popular meme, or even build something more elaborate, such as a 404 mini-game. Although it’s <em>technically</em> not a 404 page, Google’s \"No internet\" dinosaur game is a good example of how you can transform an error page into something fun and engaging.</p><p>However, your 404 page should always be appropriate for your target audience and your wider website. A humorous 404 page may not be appropriate if your website covers sensitive topics, or if you’re trying to present yourself as a trusted authority.</p><h4>Re-Engage Disengaged Visitors <br></h4><p>There are many different ways that a visitor can arrive at your 404 page, but the end result is always the same: this person expected to access some interesting content, and now they’re staring at an error message. They’re likely to be frustrated and annoyed, and may even be on the verge of giving up on your website entirely.&nbsp;</p><p>A custom 404 page is an opportunity to recapture this person’s interest before they navigate away from your website.</p><p>You can often re-engage a disappointed visitor by featuring&nbsp;navigational controls that promote your website’s most interesting and relevant content. These controls might include menus, carousels, a list of your site’s most popular pages, or a list of recommended posts based on the content they've previously accessed.</p><p>By signposting your website’s most interesting content, your 404 page can encourage visitors to dive back into your website, rather than navigating away from it.&nbsp;</p><h4>Drive Conversions and Close Sales <br></h4><p>Why not use your 404 page as a tool to drive conversions and secure additional sales?&nbsp;</p><p>You could offer a discount, coupon code, or a free <a href=\"https://webdesign.tutsplus.com/tutorials/15-membership-plugins-adding-members-to-your-wordpress-site--cms-30232?_ga=2.218894553.1939968695.1595426321-656173759.1592834457\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">membership subscription</a> as an apology, or even a reward for “finding” your 404 page!</p><p>Alternatively, if you operate an <a href=\"https://code.tutsplus.com/tutorials/how-to-build-an-amazon-affiliate-website-with-a-woocommerce-affiliate-plugin--cms-33154\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">eCommerce store</a>, then why not add some product recommendations to your 404 page? Bonus points if these recommendations are tailored for the individual visitor.&nbsp;</p><h4>Build Trust With a Consistent Brand Image <br></h4><p>Studies show that once you’re familiar with a company’s branding, you subconsciously start to trust that company. Consistency is the key to consumer confidence, which explains why every Apple store around the world looks eerily similar.</p><p>After investing so much time and effort into designing a website that perfectly reflects your brand, the last thing you want is for a generic 404 page to pop up and completely ruin the mood.</p><p>By creating a custom 404 page, you can deliver a seamless user experience, reinforce your brand, and instill a sense of trust in your target audience.&nbsp;</p><h4>Transform Lost Visitors Into Invaluable Testers<br></h4><p>When it comes to identifying and fixing broken links, why not enlist the help of your audience?</p><p>Simply add a contact form to your 404 page, and your visitors can give you a heads-up about any broken links they discover. You could even provide an incentive for visitors to report 404 errors, such as offering a discount code or a free subscription to your <a href=\"https://webdesign.tutsplus.com/tutorials/15-membership-plugins-adding-members-to-your-wordpress-site--cms-30232?_ga=2.218894553.1939968695.1595426321-656173759.1592834457\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">members-only content</a>.</p><h2>What Is Elementor?<br></h2><p>Throughout this tutorial, we’ll be using Elementor to build advanced page layouts using a simple drag-and-drop editor.&nbsp;</p><p>The core Elementor plugin is free to download and provides access to over 40 basic Elementor widgets and over 30 templates. However, if you invest in a premium plan, then you’ll also get access to Elementor’s:</p><ul><li><strong>Theme Builder</strong>. This allows you to customize your entire WordPress theme, including its header, footer, and archive pages.&nbsp;</li><li><strong>Popup Builder</strong>. Popups may get a bad reputation, but the occasional well-placed popup can be a great way to catch the visitor’s attention. Using the Popup Builder, you can design, test, and publish custom popups via the familiar Elementor user interface.&nbsp;</li><li><strong>WooCommerce Builder</strong>. If you’re building an eCommerce store, then the WooCommerce builder provides eCommerce-themed widgets that you can drag and drop into your store, including <strong>Add to Cart</strong>, <strong>Product Rating</strong>, and <strong>Related Products&nbsp;</strong>widgets.&nbsp;</li></ul><p>In this tutorial, we’ll be using <a href=\"https://elementor.com/pricing/\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Elementor Pro</a>, which at the time of writing was priced between $4.10 and $16.60 per month.</p><p>If you’re using the free Elementor plugin, then this tutorial will show you how to master the Elementor user interface and workflow. However, you <em>will</em> need an <a href=\"https://elementor.com/pricing/\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Elementor Pro subscription</a> in order to complete all sections of this tutorial.&nbsp;</p><h2>How to Install Elementor for WordPress<br></h2><p>Elementor Pro requires the free version of Elementor, so first we need to install and activate this free plugin:</p><ul><li>Log in to your WordPress account, if you haven’t already.&nbsp;</li><li>In WordPress’s left-hand menu, select <strong>Plugins &gt; Add New</strong>.</li><li>Search for the <strong>Elementor</strong>&nbsp;plugin.</li><li>When the plugin appears, select <strong>Install Now &gt; Activate</strong>.</li><li>The free version of Elementor has now been added to your WordPress account.</li></ul><p>To upgrade to Elementor Pro:&nbsp;</p><ul><li>Head over to the Elementor website, and <a href=\"https://elementor.com/pricing/\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">purchase Elementor Pro</a>.</li><li>On the <a href=\"https://my.elementor.com/\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Elementor website</a>, log in to your account using the details contained in your purchase confirmation email.&nbsp;</li><li>Select <strong>Download plugin</strong>. Elementor Pro will now be downloaded as a ZIP file.&nbsp;</li></ul><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"If you havent already setup Elementor then youll need to purchase and download the Elementor Pro plugin\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-page-download-pro.png\"></figure><ul><li>Head over to your WordPress website.&nbsp;</li><li>In the left-hand menu, select <strong>Plugins &gt; Upload Plugin</strong>.</li><li>Click <strong>Choose file</strong>&nbsp;and then select the ZIP file that you just downloaded.</li><li>Select <strong>Install Now</strong>.</li><li>When prompted, click <strong>Activate Now</strong>.</li><li>You should now see a message asking you to activate your license; click <strong>Connect &amp; Activate</strong> and select <strong>Activate</strong>.</li><li>Log in to your Elementor account, if prompted.&nbsp;</li></ul><p>Elementor Pro is now set up and ready for you to use!&nbsp;</p><h2>Custom 404 Pages Without the Hassle: Elementor's Ready-Made Templates <br></h2><p>Elementor comes with a selection of ready-made templates that you can use as the basis for your WordPress pages.&nbsp;</p><p>Since it’s the easiest way to create a 404 page, we’ll base our first 404 page around one of Elementor’s templates:</p><ul><li>In WordPress’s left-hand menu, select <strong>Templates &gt; Theme Builder</strong>.</li><li>Select the <strong>Single</strong>&nbsp;tab. In Elementor, a single page is usually an individual post.</li></ul><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Well be creating a single post so select Templates  Theme Builder  Singles\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-page-create-first-single.png\"></figure><ul><li>Select <strong>Add New Single</strong>.</li><li>Open the <strong>Template type&nbsp;</strong>dropdown and select <strong>Single</strong>.</li><li>Open the <strong>Select Post Type</strong>&nbsp;dropdown and select <strong>404 page</strong>.</li></ul><p>Give your template a descriptive name. When naming your template, don’t begin the name with <strong>404</strong>&nbsp;as the resulting permalink will redirect visitors to your homepage and not your 404 page.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"You can name your 404 template anything - just dont start that name with the numbers 404\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-page-create-template.png\"></figure><p>Click <strong>Create template</strong>. Elementor Pro will now display all the available 404 templates; select the template that you want to use.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"You can use any of Elementor Pros ready-made 404 templates\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-page-template-library.jpg\"></figure><p>Whenever you choose a template, Elementor will prompt you to import the document settings for that page, which will override any previous settings for your 404 page. Unless you have a specific reason not to, you’ll generally want to import the document settings for your chosen template.&nbsp;</p><p>At this point, you have the 404 template open in the Elementor editor.&nbsp;</p><p>Since this is our first taste of Elementor, let’s take a few moments to master the editor’s fundamentals, before we start work on our 404 page.&nbsp;</p><h3>Exploring the Elementor Page Editor <br></h3><p>The Elementor live editor is divided into two sections:&nbsp;</p><h4>1. Live Preview Canvas</h4><p>To the right is the live preview canvas, where you can add widgets such as text, images, and buttons. You can also edit your widgets by changing their size and position, or remove unwanted widgets from your layout.&nbsp;</p><p>You add widgets to a page by placing them inside a wrapped box called a <em>section</em>. If you select a section in the live preview canvas, then Elementor will outline that section using a blue border.&nbsp;</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"You can build your page design in the Elementor live frontend editor\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-page-border-section.png\"></figure><p>Each section contains one or more columns. If you click to select a column, then the live preview editor will outline that column in grey and display an icon in the column’s upper-left corner.&nbsp;</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Each section consists of one or more columns which are outlined in a dotted grey line when selected \" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-column-page.png\"></figure><p>If you click to select a widget, then the live preview canvas will outline that widget using a solid blue border.&nbsp;</p><h4>2. Elementor Panel</h4><p>The Elementor Panel contains all the widgets that you can add to your page. Simply find the widget that you want to add, drag it from the Elementor Panel, and then drop it onto the live preview canvas.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"To the left side of the screen is the Elementor Panel where youll find all of Elementors ready-made widgets\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-panel.png\"></figure><p>The Elementor Panel also contains various menus, sliders, and other settings that you can use to edit your widgets, such as selecting a new font for your text, adding a border to an image, or adding a color overlay.&nbsp;</p><p>When you select a widget in the live preview canvas, the Elementor Panel will display all the settings that are relevant for the selected widget. For example, if I select the <strong>Title&nbsp;</strong>widget, then the Elementor Panel will display all the settings related to editing text.&nbsp;</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"The Elementor Panel updates based on the currently-selected widget\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-page-title-widget.png\"></figure><h3>Elementor Fundamentals: Building Your First Section <br></h3><p>Let’s look at how you can use the live preview canvas and Elementor panel to create a simple section consisting of multiple columns and widgets:&nbsp;</p><p>Add a new section, by clicking the little <strong>+</strong>&nbsp;button.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Elementor pages are made up of sections \" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-drag-widget-here.png\"></figure><p>Choose a structure for this section, which can either be a single column or multiple columns.&nbsp;<br></p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"When you create a section youll need to specify a structure for that section Elementor sections consists or one or multiple columns\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-select-structure.png\"></figure><p>At this point, you have a new section and a column—let’s add some widgets!&nbsp;</p><ul><li>In the Elementor Panel, select the dotted icon in the upper-right corner.</li><li>Make sure the <strong>Elements</strong>&nbsp;tab is selected. You should now see a list of all the available widgets.&nbsp;</li><li>Find the widget that you want to use, and drag and drop this widget into your section.&nbsp;</li><li>In the live preview editor, click to select your widget; the Elementor Panel will now display all the settings that you can use to customize this widget.&nbsp;</li><li>Let’s add a second widget! In the Elementor Panel, click to select the dotted icon in the upper-right corner, and make sure the <strong>Elements</strong>&nbsp;tab is selected.</li><li>Choose a second widget, and drop it into your section.&nbsp;</li></ul><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Using Elementor you can build complex pages simply by adding widgets to sections\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-basic-section-widgets.png\"></figure><p>You now have a simple section consisting of two widgets. There are a few ways in which you can edit this section:</p><h4>Drag and Drop to a New Location<br></h4><p>You can move this section to a new location.</p><p>Just hover over the section until the live preview canvas outlines the section in blue and displays three handles. Then grab the middle handle (circled in the following screenshot).</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"You can drag a section to a new location by grabbing its blue handles\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-relocate-section.png\"></figure><p>Drag this section to a new location and release.&nbsp;<br></p><h4>Delete a Section</h4><p>Made a terrible mistake? You can delete a section and all of its widgets by <strong>Control-clicking</strong> the section and then selecting <strong>Delete</strong>.</p><h4>Delete a Column&nbsp;</h4><p>To remove a column from your section:</p><ul><li><p>Hover over the <strong>Column</strong>&nbsp;icon (circled in the following screenshot).</p></li></ul><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"You can simplify a section by removing unwanted columns from that section\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-page-column-icon.png\"></figure><ul><li><strong>Control-click</strong> the <strong>Column</strong> icon.</li><li>Select <strong>Delete</strong>&nbsp;from the context menu that appears.</li></ul><h4>Add More Columns<br></h4><p>Unhappy with a section’s layout? It’s easy to add more columns:</p><ul><li><strong>Control-click</strong> the <strong>Column&nbsp;</strong>icon.</li><li>Select <strong>Add New Column</strong>. A new column will now be added to this section.&nbsp;</li></ul><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Even if youve selected a single-column structure you can add extra columns to your section\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-new-column.png\"></figure><p>When a section consists of multiple columns, you can resize your columns by dragging their dividing line.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"You can resize a column by dragging the line that divides this column from the next\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-resize-column.png\"></figure><p>Using these simple techniques, you can build complex page layouts—simply keep adding sections, columns, and widgets, and tweaking their settings until you’re happy with the results.</p><h2>How to Customize Elementor's Ready-Made Templates <br></h2><p>At this point, we’ve created a 404 page using a template.&nbsp;</p><p>Depending on your chosen template, customizing this 404 page may be as simple as tweaking some of its text and hitting <strong>Publish</strong>. However, to make things more interesting I’ll cover a few widgets that you may want to add to your 404 page, even when you’re using a ready-made template.</p><h3>Help Visitors Navigate Your Site <br></h3><p>If you've already created a few menus for your website,&nbsp;then adding these menus to your 404 page can help create a consistent look and feel.</p><p>Elementor provides a&nbsp;<strong>Navigation menu&nbsp;</strong>widget.&nbsp;</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"You can use the Navigation menu widget to create a simple bullet-point menu \" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-navigation-menu.png\"></figure><p>To set up a&nbsp;<strong>Navigation menu</strong>&nbsp;widget:&nbsp;<br></p><ul><li>In the Elementor Panel, select <strong>Navigation menu</strong>&nbsp;and drop this widget into a section.&nbsp;</li><li>Click to select the navigation menu widget that you just created.</li><li>In the Elementor Panel, open the <strong>Select Menu</strong>&nbsp;dropdown.</li><li>You should now see a list of all the menus you’ve created for your website; select the menu that you want to use.</li></ul><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Add any of your websites menus to your 404 page using the Navigation menu widget\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-configure-nav-menu.png\"></figure><ul><li>In the <strong>Title</strong>&nbsp;textbox, give this menu an optional title.</li><li>When you’re happy with how your menu is configured, click <strong>Apply</strong>.&nbsp;</li></ul><p>Alternatively, you can use Elementor’s <strong>New menu</strong>&nbsp;widget.</p><h3>Add a Search Bar <br></h3><p>You can help visitors find <em>exactly </em>the content they're interested in, by adding a search bar to your 404 page.</p><p>You can create a basic search field using Elementor’s <strong>Search</strong>&nbsp;widget.&nbsp;</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"You can let visitors search for exactly the content they had in mind using Elementors Search widget\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-search-bar.png\"></figure><p>In the Elementor Panel, find the <strong>Search</strong>&nbsp;widget, drop it onto the desired section, and then click <strong>Apply</strong>.&nbsp;</p><h3>Publishing Your First Custom 404 Page <br></h3><p>Once you’re happy with the changes you’ve made to your template, it’s time to publish your 404 page:</p><ul><li>In the Elementor Panel, select <strong>Publish</strong>.</li><li>In the subsequent popup, open the <strong>Include</strong>&nbsp;dropdown and make sure <strong>404 page</strong>&nbsp;is selected.&nbsp;</li></ul><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"When asked Where do youw ant to display your template select Include 404 page\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-publish-404.png\"></figure><ul><li><p>Click <strong>Save and close</strong>.</p></li></ul><p>You can now see your 404 page in action by deliberately entering an incorrect URL or using the following URL: <a>www.(your-website-url)/404</a>.</p><h2>Designing a 404 Page With Elementor's Theme Builder</h2><p>Perhaps you have a specific vision in mind; maybe you want to ensure your 404 page stands out from the crowd, or maybe you want to experiment with lots of different potential designs? In this section, we’ll build a 404 page from scratch, using Elementor’s Theme Builder.</p><p>Elementor Pro’s Theme Builder lets you customize every part of your WordPress theme, including areas that would normally require you to know CSS and PHP—or have a developer friend who’s willing to help you out!&nbsp;</p><p>Note that in the following screenshots I’m using the <a href=\"https://unblast.com/free-404-error-page-donut-template-ai/\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Donut Template graphic</a>. This resource is free to download, although the designer has a PayPal donation link if you want to thank them for their hard work.</p><p>To create a 404 page using Elementor’s Template Builder, first head over to the main WordPress dashboard. In the left-hand menu, select <strong>Templates </strong>and click&nbsp;<strong>Add New</strong>.</p><p>Open the <strong>Template type</strong>&nbsp;dropdown and select <strong>Single</strong>. Then, in the&nbsp;<strong>Select post type</strong>&nbsp;dropdown, choose <strong>404 page</strong>.</p><p>Give your template a descriptive name and click <strong>Create template</strong>. This will launch Elementor’s template library. Since we’re not using another template as a starting point, just&nbsp;close this window. You should now have a completely blank slate to work with.&nbsp;</p><p>Add your first section by clicking the little <strong>Add New Section</strong>&nbsp;icon. You can now choose a structure for this section; I’m using a single column.&nbsp;</p><p>Click to select the section that you just created and now, in the Elementor Panel, open the <strong>Content width</strong>&nbsp;dropdown and select <strong>Full width</strong>.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Make sure your section takes up the entire width of the screen\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-content-width.png\"></figure><p>Open the <strong>Height</strong>&nbsp;dropdown, and select <strong>Fit to screen</strong>.</p><p>Next, select the Elementor Panel’s <strong>Style</strong>&nbsp;tab.&nbsp;Click to expand the <strong>Background</strong>&nbsp;section. You can now set the background for your 404 page. You can choose from an image, gradient, video, or a solid color. I’ve opted for a plain white background, by selecting <strong>Classic&nbsp;</strong>and then choosing white in the color picker.&nbsp;</p><p>Now that we have our background sorted, let’s add an image! In the live preview canvas, click the little <strong>+</strong>&nbsp;icon. Then, in the Elementor Panel, find the <strong>Image</strong>&nbsp;widget and drop it onto your section.&nbsp;</p><p>Select the Elementor Panel’s <strong>Content</strong>&nbsp;tab and click <strong>Choose image</strong>&nbsp;and select the image that you want to display as part of your 404 page.&nbsp;You can now use the Elementor Panel to resize your image (I’m using 2048x2048) and change where the image appears within your section.&nbsp;</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Use the Elementor Panel to increase or decrease the size of your image widget \" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-building-custom-404.png\"></figure><p>Next, I want to add some text explaining that this is a 404 page. In the Elementor Panel, find the <strong>Heading</strong>&nbsp;widget and drag it&nbsp;towards the section that contains your image; a blue panel should appear, indicating where this widget will appear when dropped.&nbsp;</p><p>I’m adding the <strong>Heading</strong>&nbsp;widget directly below my image.&nbsp;</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Add some text to your 404 page by grabbing the Heading widget and dropping it onto your template\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-page-heading-widget.png\"></figure><p>In the Elementor Panel, make sure the <strong>Content</strong>&nbsp;tab is selected. Then, in the <strong>Title</strong>&nbsp;textbox, enter the text that you want to use.&nbsp;</p><p>You can now use the&nbsp;<strong>Style</strong>&nbsp;tab in the Elementor Panel to change the text’s appearance, including its size and alignment. In this tab, you can change the text’s color and font, add a shadow, and make other stylistic changes. Spend some time experimenting to see what effects you can create.</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Create more beautiful text bya dding effects such as shadows changing the typography or selecting a new color \" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-custom-page404.png\"></figure><p>When you’re happy with your text, reset the Elementor Panel by selecting the dotted icon in its upper-right corner. In the Elementor Panel, find the button widget and drop this widget onto a section; I’m placing my button directly beneath my <strong>Heading&nbsp;</strong>widget.&nbsp;</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Im going to add a button that links through to my homepage\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/369/posts/35555/image/elementor-wordpress-404-page-button.png\"></figure><p>In the Elementor Panel, select the <strong>Content</strong>&nbsp;tab.&nbsp;In <strong>Link</strong>, enter the desired location—for example, I’m linking to my website’s homepage.&nbsp;You can add an optional label to your button using the <strong>Text</strong>&nbsp;field; I’m using <strong>Go home</strong>.&nbsp;</p><p>You can now style your button, e.g. by changing its size and where it’s positioned within the section.&nbsp;Select the Elementor Panel’s <strong>Style</strong>&nbsp;tab and make any subsequent stylistic changes. For example, I’m changing the button’s color to complement the rest of my 404 page.&nbsp;</p><p>Once you’re happy with your 404 page, it’s time to publish:</p><ul><li>In the Elementor Panel, select <strong>Publish</strong>.</li><li>Open the <strong>Include</strong>&nbsp;dropdown and select <strong>404 page</strong>.</li><li>Click <strong>Save &amp; Close</strong>.</li></ul><p>Your 404 page is now live! You can see your 404 page in action, either by visiting a URL that you know doesn’t exist or by heading over to <a href=\"https://www.(your-website-url)/404.\">www.(your-website-url)/404</a>.<br></p><h2>Web Design Made Easier, With Template Kits<br></h2><p>Why restrict yourself to one template, when you can install an entire template kit?</p><p>Elementor template kits, found on&nbsp;<a href=\"https://elements.envato.com/wordpress/compatible-with-elementor\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">Envato Elements</a>, are themed collections of templates that provide all the pages your website could possibly need, including the homepage, <strong>Contact Us</strong>&nbsp;page, blog, archive, <strong>About Us</strong>&nbsp;page, and much more.</p><p>If you want to mix and match, then template kits also provide stand-alone blocks that you can drag and drop into your page layouts to create your own unique designs.&nbsp;</p><p>Template kits can take the pain out of designing and building a WordPress website. Simply choose your kit, generate all the required pages, make a few customizations, and then connect these pages together—and congratulations, you have a new website!&nbsp;</p><p>Alternatively, you can use template kits to enhance an existing website, by adding designs and layouts that give your website an entirely new look and feel, with minimal effort.</p><p>Envato Elements provides a wide range of professionally designed template kits, ranging from flexible, multipurpose templates to industry-specific kits that were designed with your niche firmly in mind—whether that’s <a href=\"https://elements.envato.com/petcare-pet-boarding-and-care-centre-template-kit-4RAUEW8\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">pet boarding</a>, <a href=\"https://elements.envato.com/khubi-dermatologist-skin-care-template-kit-V6MNLC5\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">skincare</a>, <a href=\"https://elements.envato.com/dma-digital-marketing-agency-template-kit-JBPWQ3V\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">digital marketing</a>, <a href=\"https://elements.envato.com/eis-ice-cream-shop-template-kit-BNJRPYG\" rel=\"external\" target=\"_blank\">ice cream</a>, or anything in between!&nbsp;</p><p>In my next post, I’ll show you how to create a 404 page using the Envato template kit of your choice. Since we’re working with a full template kit, after completing this section you’ll have access to a range of complementary templates covering all the most common webpages—perfect if you like your new 404 page so much that you decide to expand its design to other areas of your website!&nbsp;</p><h2>Conclusion&nbsp;</h2><p>In this tutorial, I covered three ways that you can use Elementor to build a custom 404 page. If you are on a tight budget, you might not be able to afford to purchase these premium email plugins. This should not stop you from integrating your email service provider with your WooCommerce website. </p><p>Below are a collection of the five best free email and Mailchimp WooCommerce WordPress plugins available.</p><h3>1. <a href=\"https://wordpress.org/plugins/sumome/\" target=\"_self\">Sumo</a>\n</h3><p>Sumo is a powerful tool to help you grow your email list, increase conversions, and generate more sales for your online businesses. However, once you hit a certain number of customers, you will have to pay to use the plugin and its premium features. </p><h3>2. <a href=\"https://wordpress.org/plugins/mailchimp-for-wp/\" target=\"_self\">Mailchimp for WordPress</a>\n</h3><p>This Mailchimp WordPress integration plugin helps you create opt-in forms, grow your email list, and create more targeted audiences for you to market to. One powerful feature that can be implemented is a checkbox for customers to subscribe to your WordPress newsletter on checkout. </p><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"Mailchimp for WordPress\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1809/posts/34341/image/screenshot-6.png\"></figure><h3>3. <a href=\"https://wordpress.org/plugins/icegram/\" target=\"_self\">Icegram</a><br>\n</h3><p>Icegram is not your typical opt-in list building plugin. This plugin is focused on lead generation. You will find features like call to action buttons, appealing slide-in messengers, popups, and welcome bars.</p><h3>4. <a href=\"https://wordpress.org/plugins/wp-subscribe/\" target=\"_self\">WP Subscribe</a>\n</h3><figure class=\"post_image\"><img alt=\"WP Subscribe\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1809/posts/34341/image/Untitled-1.png\"></figure><p>This all-in-one email WooCoomerce plugin integrates with AWeber, Mailchimp, and FeedBurner. You can create eye-catching opt-in forms like the one above with this free plugin. </p><h3>5. <a href=\"https://wordpress.org/plugins/jetpack/\" target=\"_self\">Jetpack</a>\n</h3><p>This popular security and performance plugin has a few tricks up its sleeve. You can use the plugin to display a pop-up window for both email and WordPress newsletter subscriptions. </p><h2>Optional Sections for Your Marketing Emails<br>\n</h2><h3>1. Use Opt-In Forms</h3><p>One of your biggest assets as an eCommerce store is your email list. Email lists provide a direct connection to your potential and existing customers. By adding opt-in forms to your website, you will be able to collect emails and market with a WooCommerce Mailchimp subscribe list. One effective way to collect emails from this opt-in form is to offer a free download in return for the user's email address. </p><figure class=\"post_image\"><a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/woochimp-woocommerce-mailchimp-integration/6044286\" target=\"_self\"><img alt=\"WooChimp Constructing Form\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1809/posts/34341/image/ad.png\"></a><figcaption>Creating an email opt-in form in the WP dashboard for the WooChimp plugin.</figcaption></figure><h3>2. Tag Your Email Subscribers</h3><p>As mentioned, no matter what type of WooCommerce website you are running, you will want to have opt-in forms to collect emails. The user emails collected should then be tagged in your email service provider so you can engage them in a targeted marketing plan in the future. </p><p>For example, if you are running an online clothing store and offer a free coupon for a discount on a pair of jeans, then you should tag the users that sign up on this opt-in form as \"Interested In Jeans.\" Then you can send specific emails on a new release of jeans or other discounts on jeans and the marketing campaign will be much more successful as the user had already shown interest in the jeans that were on your website. <br></p><h3>3. Customize Your Email Templates <br>\n</h3><p>As a business, you will want to take advantage of every opportunity to promote your brand. Every piece of content the customer or potential customer sees should reflect your brand identity. This includes the transactional WooCommerce emails that are sent out. When customizing the transactional emails, you will want to ensure that the company's logo is present as well as the brand's colors and fonts. </p><p>In another tutorial, I show <a href=\"https://code.tutsplus.com/tutorials/create-branded-woocommerce-emails-with-email-customizer-plugins--cms-33912\" target=\"_self\">step by step how to create branded WooCommerce emails</a>.</p><ul class=\"roundup-block__contents posts--half-width roundup-block--list\"><li class=\"roundup-block__content\"><a class=\"roundup-block__content-link\" href=\"https://code.tutsplus.com/tutorials/create-branded-woocommerce-emails-with-email-customizer-plugins--cms-33912\"><img class=\"roundup-block__preview-image\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1809/posts/33912/preview_image/Untitled-2.jpg\"><div class=\"roundup-block__primary-category topic-code\">WordPress Plugins</div>\n<div class=\"roundup-block__content-title\">Create Branded WooCommerce Emails With an Email Customizer Plugin </div>\n<div class=\"roundup-block__author\">Daniel Strongin</div></a></li></ul><p>While this may seem like only a minor change to the email templates, it will have a huge impact on the customer's perception of your brand.  replace me</p><figure class=\"post_image\"><a href=\"https://codecanyon.net/item/email-customizer-for-woocommerce/8654473\" target=\"_self\"><img alt=\"Email Customizer for WooCommerce Customize Email Template\" src=\"https://cms-assets.tutsplus.com/uploads/users/1809/posts/34341/image/em.png\"></a><figcaption>Customizing the \"received order\" email template</figcaption></figure><h3>4. Remind Your Customers and Potential Customers</h3><p>Sending out an email inviting your customers and potential customers to purchase your products on a random schedule is not going to cut it here. You need to make sure you are taking advantage of every opportunity to market to your customers by sending out dedicated emails based on their actions. Here are a few scenarios when you would want to send out a custom email to encourage your customers to make a purchase:</p><ul>\n<li>when they abandon their cart</li>\n<li>when they sign up on one of your opt-in forms</li>\n<li>when a potential customer has not made a purchase in a specific number of weeks</li>\n</ul><p>Sending out these WooCommerce subscription reminder emails and similar messages can help engage with leads you don't want to lose.</p><h2>5 Common Questions Everyone Has About Email Marketing</h2><p>The Mailchimp and WooCommerce plugins can help drive conversions, but learning more about email marketing can push those numbers sky-high.
